نذر مطلق ، مانی اس کا پورا کرنا لازم ہے یہی حکم نذارمعین کا ہے
مَنْ نَذَرَ نَذَرًا مُطْلَقًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاءُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ نَذَرَ وَسَمَّى فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاءُ بِمَا سَمَّى وَ إِنْ عَلَّقَ النَّذْرَ بِشَرْطٍ فَوُجِدَ الشَّرْطُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاءُ بِنَفْسِ النَّذْرِ لِإِطْلَاقِ الْحَدِيثِ وَلاَنَّ الْمُعَلَّقَ بِشَرْطٍ كَالْمُنْجَزِ عِنْدَهُ وَعَنْ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّهُ رَجَعَ عَنْهُ وَقَالَ إِذَا قَالَ إِنْ فَعَلْتُ كَذَا فَعَلَيَّ حَجَّةٌ أَوْ صَوْمُ سَنَةٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةُ مَالِ أَهْلَكَهُ أَجْزَأَهُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ كَفَّارَةُ يَمِيْنٍ وَهُوَ قَوْلُ مُحَمَّدٍ وَيَخْرُجُ عَنِ الْعُهْدَةِ بِالْوَفَاءِ بِمَا سَمَّى أَيْضًا وَهَذَا إِذَا كَانَ شَرْطًا لاَ يُرِيدُ كَوْنَهُ لِأَنَّ فِيهِ مَعْنَى الْيَمِينِ وَهُوَ الْمَنْعُ وَهُوَ بِظَاهِرِهِ نَذَرْ فَيَتَخَيَّرُ وَيَمِيلُ إِلَى أَيِّ الْجِهَتَيْنِ شَاءَ بِخِلاَفِ مَا إِذَا كَانَ شَرْطًا يُرِيدُ كَوْنَهُ كَقَوْلِهِ إِنْ شَفَى اللَّهُ مَرِيضِى لِانْعِدَامِ مَعْنَى الْيَمِينِ فِيهِ وَ هُوَ الْمَنْعُ وَهَذَا التَّفْصِيلُ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے نذر مطلق کی یعنی کسی قید و شرط کے بغیر تو اس پر اسے پورا کرنا واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس شخص نے نذر کی اور اس نذر کو بیان کر دیا تو جو کچھ بیان کیا اس کو ادا کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ اور اگر نذر کو کسی شرط کے ساتھ معلق کیا یعنی مثلا فلاں بیمار اچھا ہو جائے تو مجھ پر حج لازم ہے۔ پھر وہ شرط پائی گئی تو نذر کو پورا کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حدیث کے مطلق ہونے میں یہ بھی داخل ہے۔ اور اس وجہ سے بھی کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک شرطیہ نذر کرنا غیر شرطیہ نذر کرنے کے مانند ہے۔ اور یہ بھی ایک روایت ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ نے اس قول سے رجوع کر لیا ہے۔ اور کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اس طرح کہا کہ اگر میں ایسا کروں تو مجھ پر حج یا ایک سال کے روزے یا ایسے مال کا صدقہ جس کا میں مالک ہوں واجب ہے۔ تو اس میں قسم کا کفارہ دینا کافی ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد کا یہی قول ہے اور اگر وہی بات یا چیز پوری کر دی جو بیان کی تھی یعنی حج یا روزہ وغیرہ تو ستم کے ذمہ سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہ بات اسی وقت ہوگی کہ جب یہ شرط ایسی ہو کہ جس کا ہونا اسے منظور نہ ہو۔ یعنی مثلاً اگر میں شراب پیوں حالانکہ وہ شراب پینا نہ چاہتا ہوتو یہ تم ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس میں قسم کے معنی یعنی باز رہے کے پائے جارہے ہیں۔ اگر چہ ظاہر لفظ کے اعتبار سے یہ نذر ہے۔ اس لئے اسے یہ اختیار دیا گیا ہے کہ اگر چاہے تو کفارہ دیدے۔ اور چاہے تو جو کچھ کہا ہے اس کو پورا کرے۔ کیونکہ ایک اعتبار سے یہ قسم ہے۔ تو دوسرے اعتبار سے یہ نذر ہے۔ اس لئے اسے یہ اختیار ہے کہ جسے چاہے قبول کر لے اور اگر اس کے برخلاف ایسی شرط ہو کہ جس کا پایا جانا اسے پسند ہو مثلاً اگر یوں کہا کہ اگر اللہ میرے بیمار کو شفادے تو مجھ پر حج یا روزہ یا صدقہ لازم ہے۔ اس طرح کہنے سے یہ فقط نذر ہوگی۔ کیونکہ اس میں قسم کے معنی نہیں ہیں یعنی باز رہنا نہیں پایا جارہا ہے۔ یہی تفصیل صحیح ہے۔
تشریح
فائده ... یعنی اگر ایسی شرط ہو کہ جس کے ہونے کو وہ پسند کرتا ہوتو وہ فقط نذر ہوگی اور اگر ایسی شرط ہو کہ جس کے ہونے کو وہ پسند نہیں کرتا ہو تو اس میں باز رہنا پایا جاتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس میں ایک اعتبار سے نذر اور دوسرے اعتبار سے قسم ہے۔ لہذا اگر چاہے تو نذر ادا کر دے یا چاہے تو قسم کا کفارہ ادا کردے)۔ ٤ وَ مَنْ نَذَرَ نَشْرًا مُطْلَقًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاءُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ نَذَرَوَسَمَّى فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاء بِمَاسَم ... الخ اگر کسی نذر مطلق کی یعنی کسی قید و شرط کے بغیر تو اس پر اسے پورا کرنا واجب ہے۔ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے اس فرمان کی وجہ سے کہ جس شخص نے نذر کی اور بیان کر دی تو جو کچھ بیان کیا اسے پورا کرنا واجب ہے۔ فائدہ یہ حدیث غریب ہے۔ اگر چہ اس بارے میں حدیثیں بہت ہیں۔ ان میں سے ایک یہ بھی ہے جو حضرت ابن عباس رضی اللہ تعالیٰ عنہ سے مروی ہے اس کے آخر میں ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا تو اس کا قرض ادا کرنا ( کیا ضروری نہیں ہے ) سائل نے عرض کیا کہ ہاں (ضروری ہے) پھر آپ نے فرمایا کہ دین الہی ادا کرنے کا زیادہ مستحق ہے۔ یعنی قرض کی ادائیگی زیادہ واجب الاداء ہے۔ (رواہ البخاری) ایک اور حدیث میں ہے کہ میں نے زمانہ جاہلیت میں یہ نذر کی تھی کہ ایک رات مسجد الحرام میں اعتکاف کروں گا۔ تو رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم اپنی نذر پوری کر لو۔ بخاری اور مسلم نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اور میں ایک اور حدیث میں ہے کہ معصیت میں نذر کی وفا نہیں ہے۔ (مسلم) ایک اور حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک عورت نے آکر عرض کی کہ یا رسول اللہ میں نے نذر کی تھی کہ آپ کی موجودگی میں دف بجاؤں گی۔ تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ اپنی نذر پوری کر لو ۔ ابوداؤد نے اس کی روایت کی ہے۔ اس حدیث میں اس بات کی دلیل ہے کے دف بجانا ممنوع نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نکاح وغیرہ میں دف سے اعلان کا حکم ہے۔ اور ایک حدیث میں ہے کہ جس نے اللہ تعالیٰ کی فرماں برداری کی نیت کی تو وہ فرماں برداری کرے۔ اور جس نے نافرمانی کی نیت کی تو وہ اس کی نافرمانی نہ کرے۔ اس کی روایت بخاری نے کی ہے۔
Absolute vow; meaning fulfilling it is obligatory; this is the ruling of a specified vow. Whoever makes an absolute vow, fulfilling it is obligatory upon him, due to the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Whoever makes a vow and specifies it, then fulfilling that which he specified is obligatory upon him.' And if he makes the vow conditional upon a condition and the condition occurs, then fulfilling the very vow is obligatory upon him, due to the generality of the hadith, and because a conditional vow is like an unconditional vow in his view. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he retracted this and said: If he says 'If I do such-and-such, then upon me is a Hajj, or a year's fast, or charity of property that I possess,' then expiation of an oath suffices for that, and this is the saying of Muhammad. And he also fulfills the obligation by fulfilling what he specified. And this is when the condition is such that he does not desire its occurrence, because in it is the meaning of an oath, which is abstention, and outwardly it is a vow. So he has the choice, leaning towards whichever of the two aspects he wishes. Contrary to when the condition is such that he desires its occurrence, like his saying 'If Allah cures my sick,' because the meaning of an oath is absent in it, and this detail is the correct one. Translation: If someone makes an absolute vow, i.e., without any condition, then fulfilling it is obligatory upon him, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said that whoever makes a vow and specifies it, then what he specified must be fulfilled. And if he suspends the vow on a condition, e.g., 'if a certain sick person recovers, then Hajj is obligatory upon me,' then the condition occurs, fulfilling the vow becomes obligatory, because it is included in the generality of the hadith, and also because in the view of Imam Abu Hanifa, a conditional vow is like an unconditional vow. And there is a narration that Imam Abu Hanifa retracted this saying and said: If someone says, 'If I do such-and-such, then upon me is Hajj, or a year's fast, or charity of property I own,' then expiation of an oath suffices for that, and this is the saying of Imam Muhammad. And he is also released from liability by fulfilling what he specified. And this is only when the condition is such that he does not desire its occurrence, e.g., 'if I drink wine' while he does not want to drink wine, then it is an oath, because the meaning of an oath, i.e., abstention, is found in it. Although outwardly it is a vow, he is given the choice: if he wishes, he can give expiation, and if he wishes, he can fulfill what he said. Because from one aspect it is an oath, and from another aspect it is a vow. So he has the choice to accept whichever he wishes. And contrary to this, if the condition is such that he desires its occurrence, e.g., he says, 'If Allah cures my sick, then upon me is Hajj, fast, or charity,' then it is solely a vow, because the meaning of an oath (abstention) is not found in it. This detail is correct. Explanation: Benefit: If the condition is such that he desires its occurrence, then it is solely a vow; if he does not desire its occurrence, then abstention is found. Therefore, from one aspect it is a vow and from another aspect it is an oath. So if he wishes, he can fulfill the vow, or if he wishes, he can give the expiation of an oath. And whoever makes an absolute vow, fulfilling it is obligatory upon him, due to the saying of the Prophet: 'Whoever makes a vow and specifies it, then fulfilling that which he specified is obligatory.' Benefit: This hadith is gharib. However, there are many hadiths on this topic. Among them is one narrated from Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him), at its end: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Is it not necessary to repay his debt?' The questioner said, 'Yes (necessary).' Then he said, 'The debt of Allah is more deserving of being repaid.' (Narrated by Bukhari). Another hadith: 'I made a vow in the time of ignorance to perform i'tikaf for one night in the Sacred Mosque.' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said, 'Fulfill your vow.' Bukhari and Muslim narrated it. Another hadith: 'There is no fulfillment of a vow in disobedience.' (Muslim). Another hadith: A woman came and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I vowed to beat the duff in your presence.' He said, 'Fulfill your vow.' Abu Dawood narrated it. This hadith indicates that beating the duff is not prohibited. Therefore, in marriage etc., announcing with the duff is commanded. Another hadith: 'Whoever intends obedience to Allah, let him perform obedience; and whoever intends disobedience, let him not disobey.' Narrated by Bukhari.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the subject of vows (nadhr). It begins by stating the default rule: an absolute vow (without condition) must be fulfilled, supported by the hadith 'man nadhara wa samma...'. Then it discusses conditional vows. Initially, it notes that according to Imam Abu Hanifa's first position, a conditional vow is treated like an unconditional vow, so fulfillment is required. However, the text then presents a reported retraction (ruju') from Abu Hanifa, where he aligns with Imam Muhammad's view: if the condition is something the person does not want to happen (like drinking wine), the expression has the nature of an oath (yamin) rather than a vow, giving the person a choice between fulfilling the specified act or giving expiation. The reasoning is that such a phrase contains the element of prevention (man'), which is characteristic of an oath. In contrast, if the condition is something desired (like recovery from illness), it is purely a vow with no oath element, so only fulfillment is valid. The correct view (as per the text) is this distinction based on the desirability of the condition. The text also includes numerous supporting hadiths from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawood, emphasizing the obligation of fulfilling vows and the prohibition of vows in disobedience. The commentary (tashrih) reiterates the distinction and the option between fulfillment and expiation.

Key Terms
نذر مطلق (nadhr mutlaq): A vow made without any condition; its fulfillment is immediately obligatory.
كفارة يمين (kaffarat yamin): Expiation for breaking an oath: feeding ten poor, clothing them, or freeing a slave. In this context, it substitutes for fulfilling the vow when the condition is disliked.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in the text, what can a person do if he says, 'If I lie, then upon me is a Hajj' (a condition he dislikes)?
A) He must perform Hajj.
B) He must give expiation of an oath.
C) He has a choice between performing Hajj or giving expiation.
D) He is not obligated to do anything because it was an oath.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on vows distinguishes between absolute and conditional vows, and within conditional vows, the desirability of the condition determines whether it is a vow or an oath with a choice.

The Rule of Istithna (Insha'Allah) in Oaths and Obligation of Absolute Vows
Ruling on absolute vows and condition for istithna in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for an absolute vow and explain the requirement of immediate connection for the exception phrase 'Insha'Allah' in oaths.

Core Idea
An absolute vow must be fulfilled; 'Insha'Allah' immunizes an oath only if said immediately.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents two rulings. First, an absolute vow (nazr mutlaq) must be fulfilled based on the hadith. Second, the exception phrase 'Insha'Allah' in an oath prevents breaking it (hanth) only if said immediately after the oath; delay is a retraction and invalidates the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the passage and note that it addresses an absolute vow and the effect of 'Insha'Allah' on an oath.
The passage contains two separate rulings.
2
For the absolute vow, find the proof
Locate the hadith cited: 'Whoever makes a vow and specifies, fulfillment is upon him.' This establishes the wajib nature of fulfilling an absolute vow.
The vow is unconditional (mutlaq) and must be fulfilled.
3
For the istithna, identify the condition
The hadith 'Whoever swears an oath and says Insha'Allah has been true to his oath' is the proof. The author stresses that connection (ittisal) is essential.
The phrase must be said immediately after the oath; delay is a retraction.
4
Understand why delay is invalid
The author explains that after completion of the oath, saying 'Insha'Allah' is a retraction, and retraction is not allowed in oaths.
No retraction in yamin, so the oath stands as broken if the condition is unmet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ما يكون يمينا و ما لا يكون يمينا
وَ مَنْ نَذَرَ نَشْرًا مُطْلَقًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاءُ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ نَذَرَوَسَمَّى فَعَلَيْهِ الْوَفَاء بِمَاسَمَّى
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ عَلَى يَمِيْنِ وَقَالَ إِنْ شَاءَ اللهُ مُتَّصِلا بِيَمِينِهِ فَلَاحِنتَ عَلَيْهِ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مَنْ حَلَفَ عَلَى يَمِيْنٍ وَقَالَ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ فَقَدْ بَرَّفِي يَمِينِهِ إِلَّا أَنَّهُ لَا بُدَّمِنَ الْإِتِصَالِ لِأَنَّهُ بَعْدَ الْفَرَاغِ رُجُوعٌ وَلَا رُجُوعَ فِي الْيَمِينِ
Chapter on what constitutes an oath and what does not. And whoever makes an absolute vow, fulfillment is incumbent upon him due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever makes a vow and specifies, fulfillment of what he specified is upon him.' He said: And whoever swears an oath and says 'If Allah wills' connected to his oath, then he is not guilty of breaking his oath due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever swears an oath and says 'If Allah wills' has indeed fulfilled his oath,' except that connection is necessary because after completion it is a retraction, and there is no retraction in an oath.
Source pages p. 68

Commentary
This passage addresses two related topics: conditional vows and the effect of the exception phrase 'Insha'Allah' on an oath. First, the author distinguishes between a conditional vow where the condition is disliked (e.g., 'If I drink wine...' which combines an oath and a vow) versus a condition that is liked (e.g., 'If Allah cures my patient...' which is a pure vow). In the first case, the person has a choice: either fulfill the vow or pay kaffarah for an oath, because the underlying intent of restraint (yamin) is present. In the second case, only a vow exists, so fulfillment is required. The ruling on absolute vows (nazr mutlaq) is that the vower must fulfill it, supported by the hadith that whoever vows and specifies must fulfill. Second, the book discusses the exception (istithna) of 'Insha'Allah' in oaths. If the phrase is uttered immediately after the oath, the person is not considered a breaker (hanith) due to the hadith: 'Whoever swears an oath and says Insha'Allah has been true to his oath.' However, connection (ittisal) is essential because saying it later is a retraction, and retraction in oaths is not permitted. The commentary then includes a story of Harun al-Rashid questioning Imam Abu Hanifa, who argued that allowing delayed istithna would undermine the caliph's bay'ah, as subjects could say 'Insha'Allah' to invalidate their allegiance. This illustrates the importance of immediate connection.

Key Terms
يمين (yamin): An oath: a binding affirmation by Allah (or equivalent) that one will or will not do something, implying restraint from the opposite.
نذر (nazr): A vow: an obligation to perform an act of worship created by one's own utterance, often conditional.
استثناء (istithna): The exception phrase 'Insha'Allah' said in conjunction with an oath to exempt from penalty if the oath is broken.
حنث (hanth): The state of breaking one's oath, incurring the need for kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person swears an oath and says 'Insha'Allah' after a short pause, is the oath considered broken?
A) Yes, because immediate connection is required.
B) No, because any 'Insha'Allah' suffices.
C) Yes, because intention matters more than wording.
D) No, because it is a retraction and retractions are allowed.

Key Takeaway
An absolute vow must be fulfilled; the exception phrase 'Insha'Allah' must be connected immediately to the oath to prevent breaking it.

Oath not to enter a house: entering a ruin does not break the oath
Ruling on oaths about entering a house: distinguishing general vs specific.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between general and specific oaths regarding the term 'dar' and apply the Hanafi rule that the building is a description (wasf) considered in absentia but disregarded when present.

Core Idea
In oaths, the building is just a description; the plot matters when pointed to, but in general oaths the building is essential.

This lesson examines a classical Hanafi ruling on oaths about entering a house. The key distinction is between a general oath (not to enter any house) and a specific oath (not to enter this house). The Hanafi school uses linguistic analysis to determine that 'dar' refers to the plot, not the building, but the building is considered when the oath is general. This ruling shows how context affects the application of oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note the two cases: general oath ('la yadkhula daran') vs specific oath ('la yadkhula hadhihi al-dar'). Determine the ruling for each when the building is ruined.
The first case: no hanth; second case: hanth.
2
Follow the linguistic proof
The author cites Arabic usage: 'dar amira' and 'dar ghamira' and poetry. This shows 'dar' is primarily the plot (arsa), and the building is a description (wasf).
Proof is from language (qawl Sahabi not needed).
3
Apply the rule to absent vs present
When the house is pointed to (present), the description is 'laghw' (disregarded) because the reference is fixed. When absent (general), the description is 'mu'tabar' (considered) to define what is meant.
This is the core of the distinction.
4
Note the practical thamarah
Thus, entering a ruin breaks a specific oath (since the plot is still that dar) but does not break a general oath (since no building exists to match the description).
The mulazim: kaffarah required only in specific case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ دَارًا فَدَخَلَ دَارًا خَرِبَةً لَمْ يَحْنَتْ وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَدَخَلَهَا بَعْدَ مَا انْهَدَمَتْ وَصَارَتْ صَحْرَاءَ حَنِثَ لِاَنَّ الدَّارَ اسْمٌ لِلْعَرْصَةِ عِنْدَ الْعَرَبِ وَالْعَجَمِ يُقَالُ دَارٌ عَامِرَةً وَدَارٌ غَامِرَةٌ وَقَدْ شَهِدَتْ أَشْعَارُ الْعَرَبِ بِذَالِكَ فَالْبِنَاءُ وَصْفٌ فِيْهَا غَيْرَ أَنَّ الْوَصْفَ فِى الْحَاضِرِ لَغْوٌ وَفِي الْغَائِبِ مُعْتَبَرٌ
And whoever swore an oath that he will not enter a house (dar), then entered a ruined house, he does not break his oath. But if he swore 'I will not enter this house', then entered it after it had collapsed and become empty land, he breaks his oath, because 'dar' is a name for the plot (arsa) among Arabs and non-Arabs. It is said 'a populated house' and 'a ruined house', and the poems of the Arabs testify to that. So the building is a description (wasf) in it, but the description in the present (referring to a specific house) is disregarded, while in the absent (non-specific) it is considered.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage states the ruling on oaths about entering a house. It distinguishes between a general oath (not to enter any house) and a specific oath (not to enter this particular house). In the first case, entering a ruin does not break the oath because the word 'dar' in general usage refers to a building, not an empty plot. In the second case, when the house is specifically pointed to, the name 'dar' applies to the plot itself, so even if the building has collapsed and become empty land, entering that land still breaks the oath. The proof is from Arabic lexicography and poetry, where 'dar' is used for both inhabited and ruined plots, and the building is merely a description. However, when a specific house is indicated by pointing (present), the description of being built is irrelevant; the oath applies to the plot. When the house is absent (not pointed to), the description is considered, so a ruin is not a 'dar'.

Key Terms
دَار (dar): A plot of land (arsa) intended for building, whether built or ruined.
عَرْصَة (arsah): Open plot of land, courtyard; the essential meaning of dar.
وَصْف (wasf): Description or attribute; here the building is considered an attribute of the dar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'I will not enter any house' (general oath) and then enters a completely ruined house with no walls or roof, does he break his oath according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) Yes, because the plot still counts as 'dar'.
B) No, because without a building it is not called 'dar' in a general oath.
C) Yes, but only if the ruin had some walls.
D) It depends on whether it was originally his house.

Key Takeaway
The ruling depends on whether the oath is general (building essential) or specific (plot suffices).

Oaths About a Specific House: Effects of Destruction and Conversion
Rulings on oath about a specific house that is destroyed and then rebuilt or turned into something else

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of name continuity (ism) to determine whether entering a rebuilt or converted property violates an oath.

Core Idea
An oath about a specific 'dar' is tied to the plot, not the structure; 'bayt' is defined by function, not form.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the subtle distinction between an oath about a 'dar' (house) and a 'bayt' (room). While the name 'dar' is attached to the plot and persists even after total collapse, 'bayt' requires the ability to stay overnight. The author also explains that converting a dar into a different type of property (mosque, bath, garden) removes the original name entirely. Understanding these principles is crucial for fiqh applications in property oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling for each scenario
Read the passage and note the rulings: (1) dar collapses and new dar built → oath broken; (2) dar converted to mosque, bath, garden, or bayt → oath not broken; (3) bayt collapses completely → oath not broken; (4) bayt walls remain but roof falls → oath broken.
2
Identify the governing principle
The name (ism) determines the application of the oath. For dar, the name is attached to the plot and survives collapse. For bayt, the name depends on the function of overnight stay (mabit); if that becomes impossible, the name is lost.
3
Trace the reasoning behind each exception
Why does conversion to a mosque remove the name? Because a new name (masjid) overrides the original. Why does bayt become non-bayt when it becomes empty land? Because no one can stay overnight there. Why does a bayt with walls but no roof remain a bayt? Because one can still stay overnight (walls provide enclosure).
4
Distinguish between dar and bayt
Note the different criteria: dar is defined by the land plot; bayt by the ability to sleep inside. This is the key analytical move.
Also: a bath or garden is clearly not a dar, but a bayt (room) could be inside a dar; the text treats bayt as a separate category.
5
Apply the rule to hypotheticals
Given new scenarios (e.g., dar becomes a school, bayt becomes a storage shed without walls), determine if the oath is broken based on whether the original name persists or is replaced.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَخَرَبَتْ ثُمَّ بُنِيَتْ أُخْرَى فَدَخَلَهَا يَحْنَتُ لِمَا ذَكَرْنَا أَنَّ الْإِسْمَ بَاقٍ بَعْدَ الْإِنْهِدَامِ وَإِنْ جُعِلَتْ مَسْجِدًا أَوْ حَمَّامًا أَوْ بُسْتَانًا أَوْ بَيْتًا فَدَخَلَهُ لَمْ يَحْنَتْ لِأَنَّهُ لَمْ يَبْقَ دَارًا بِالِاعْتِرَاضِ اسْمٍ اخَرَ عَلَيْهِ وَكَذَا إِذَا دَخَلَهُ بَعْدَ الْهِدَامِ الْحَمَّامِ وَأَشْبَاهِهِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَعُودُ اسْمُ الدَّارِ بِهِ وَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذَا الْبَيْتَ فَدَخَلَهُ بَعْدَ مَا انْهَدَمَ وَصَارَ صَحْرَاءُ لَمْ يَحْنَتْ لِزَوَالِ اسْم الْبَيْتِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُبَاتُ فِيهِ حَتَّى لَوْ بَقِيَتِ الْحَيْطَانُ وَسَقَطَ السَّقْفُ يَحْنَتُ لِأَنَّهُ يُبَاتُ فِيهِ وَالسَّقْفُ وَصْفٌ فِيهِ وَكَذَا إِذَا بُنِيَ بَيْتًا أَخَرَ فَدَخَلَهُ لَمْ يَحْنَتْ لِأَنَّ الْإِسْمَ لَمْ يَبْقَ بَعْدَ الْإِنْهِدَامِ
And if he swore 'I will not enter this house', then it collapsed and another was built, and he entered it, he breaks his oath because, as we mentioned, the name remains after collapse. But if it was made into a mosque, a bath, a garden, or a room (bayt), and he entered it, he does not break his oath because it no longer remains a house (dar) due to another name being applied to it. Likewise, if he enters it after the destruction of a bath and the like, because the name 'dar' does not return to it. And if he swore 'I will not enter this room (bayt)', then he entered it after it had collapsed and become empty land, he does not break his oath due to the removal of the name 'bayt', because one cannot stay overnight in it. However, if the walls remained and the roof fell, he breaks his oath because one can still stay overnight in it, and the roof is a description in it. Likewise, if another room (bayt) was built and he entered it, he does not break his oath because the name did not remain after collapse.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on oaths about a specific house. It clarifies that if the original house collapses and a new house is built on the same plot, the oath is broken because the name 'dar' still applies to the plot (as established earlier). However, if the plot is converted into something fundamentally different like a mosque, bath, or garden, the name 'dar' is removed, so entering does not break the oath. Similarly, if a bath collapses, it does not revert to being called 'dar'. For the word 'bayt' (room/house), the criterion is whether it can be used for overnight stay (mabit). If the walls remain but the roof collapses, it is still considered a 'bayt' because it can be slept in (under the stars?). But if it becomes completely empty land, the name is gone. Rebuilding another bayt does not revive the original name.

Key Terms
بَيْت (bayt): A room or house where one can stay overnight (yubat fihi).
مَسْجِد (masjid): A mosque; when a dar becomes a masjid, it no longer retains the name dar.
حَمَّام (hammam): A bathhouse; similar to masjid in that it replaces the name dar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears 'I will not enter this room (bayt)'. The room's roof collapses but the walls remain. He enters. Does he break his oath?
A) Yes, because the walls provide shelter and one can stay overnight.
B) No, because the roof is missing.
C) No, because it is no longer called a bayt.
D) Yes, because the plot is the same.

Key Takeaway
An oath about a specific 'dar' is violated if you enter the rebuilt structure on the same plot, but not if the plot is converted to a different use; for 'bayt', the name depends on the ability to stay overnight, not on the presence of a roof.

Oath about entering house: roof, threshold, and entrance hall
Rulings on three parts of a house in the context of an oath of entry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for standing on the roof, entering the dihliz, and standing in the threshold in the context of an oath not to enter a house, and explain the qiyas on roof and the role of custom in the dispute.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the roof is part of the house for oaths by analogy with i'tikaf; the threshold is not part if the door encloses the interior.

This passage from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar addresses a practical question: when a person swears not to enter a house, what counts as entering? The ruling distinguishes three locations: the roof (sath), the entrance hall (dihliz), and the threshold (taq al-bab). The main ruling on the roof is supported by qiyas with i'tikaf, but there is an intra-Hanafi dispute based on custom (urf). The threshold ruling depends on whether the person is inside or outside the closed door.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three locations and their default rulings
The passage discusses three places: roof (sath), entrance hall (dihliz), and threshold (taq al-bab). Identify the ruling for each: roof = hanth (oath broken), dihliz = hanth if enclosed and roofed, threshold = no hanth if standing such that closing the door leaves one outside.
For the dihliz, the ruling depends on an earlier detail about enclosure and roofing.
2
Understand the qiyas on the roof
The author uses qiyas with i'tikaf: just as going to the mosque roof does not break i'tikaf because the roof is part of the mosque, standing on the house roof counts as entering because the roof is part of the house. Trace the illa: the roof is part of the building (al-sath min al-dar).
This is qiyas jaliy with a clear illa.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on the roof
The text mentions 'qil' (it was said) that according to custom (urf), standing on the roof does not break the oath. This is a valid difference within the Hanafi school. The primary ruling from Quduri stands, but the custom-based view may apply in some regions.
Consider how custom (urf) can affect legal rulings in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the enclosure principle to the threshold
The ruling on the threshold is based on the function of the door: it encloses and secures the house. If standing in the doorway such that closing the door leaves you outside, you are not inside. So the oath is not broken.
This is a literal interpretation of 'entering' as being within the enclosed space.
5
Synthesize the three rulings
Summarize: roof = enters (by qiyas, disputed by custom); dihliz = enters if enclosed and roofed; threshold = does not enter if door, when closed, excludes you. The key principle is that 'entering' means being inside the enclosed space of the house.
The mufta bihi for roof is the primary ruling, but custom can create an exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَوَقَفَ عَلَى سَطْحِهَا حَنِثَ لِأَنَّ السَّطْحَ مِنَ الدَّارِ أَلَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْمُعْتَكِفَ لَا يَفْسُدُ اعْتِكَافُهُ بِالْخُرُوجِ إِلَى سَطْحِ الْمَسْجِدِ وَقِيلَ فِي عُرْفِنَا لَا يَحْنَثُ قَالَ وَإِذَا دَخَلَ دِهْلِيزَهَا يَحْنَثُ وَيَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَلَى التَّفْصِيلِ الَّذِي تَقَدَّمَ وَإِنْ وَقَفَ فِي طَاقِ الْبَابِ بِحَيْثُ إِذَا أُعْلِقَ الْبَابُ كَانَ خَارِجًا لَمْ يَحْنَثْ لِأَنَّ الْبَابَ لِإِحْرَازِ الدَّارِ وَمَا فِيهَا فَلَمْ يَكُنِ الْخَارِجُ مِنَ الدَّارِ
He (al-Quduri) said: Whoever swore 'I will not enter this house' and then stood on its roof, he breaks his oath because the roof is part of the house. Do you not see that the person in i'tikaf does not invalidate his i'tikaf by going out to the roof of the mosque? And it was said: in our custom, he does not break his oath. He said: If he enters its entrance hall (dihliz), he breaks his oath, and this should be subject to the detail that preceded. And if he stood in the arch of the door such that when the door is closed he would be outside, he does not break his oath because the door is for securing the house and what is in it, so what is outside is not part of the house.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage addresses whether certain parts of a house count as 'entering' for oath purposes. The established ruling from Quduri is that standing on the roof constitutes entering because the roof is considered part of the house. The proof is an analogy (qiyas) with i'tikaf: going to the roof of the mosque does not break i'tikaf, implying the roof is part of the mosque, and similarly the roof is part of the house. However, there is a differing opinion (qil) based on local custom (urf) that standing on the roof does not break the oath. Regarding the entrance hall (dihliz), the ruling depends on the earlier detail: if it is inside the house when the door is closed and roofed, it counts as part of the house; otherwise not. Finally, standing in the threshold (taq al-bab) such that when the door is closed one is outside does not break the oath, because the door is for enclosure and that area is outside the enclosure.

Key Terms
سَطْح (sath): Roof or terrace of a building.
دِهِلِيز (dihliz): Entrance hall or corridor; a covered space inside the door.
طَاق الْبَاب (taq al-bab): The archway or threshold of the door; the area within the door frame.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swears 'I will not enter this house' and then stands in the doorway (taq al-bab) such that when the door is closed he would be outside, does he break his oath?
A) Yes, because he is still within the house boundary.
B) No, because he is outside the enclosed area.
C) Yes, if the door is open.
D) It depends on his intention.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi oaths, the roof is part of the house by analogy with i'tikaf, but custom may alter the ruling; the threshold is not part of the house if the door encloses the interior.

Oath on Entering a House That Becomes Ruined or Changed
Explains rulings on oath to enter a destroyed or rebuilt house

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi definition of 'bayt' to determine whether an oath to enter a house is broken when the structure changes or is converted to another use.

Core Idea
An oath to enter a house depends on the functional identity of the building, not the land.

In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of an oath often hinges on the precise meaning of terms. The passage below from al-Quduri's matn explains that the name 'bayt' (house) is tied to its function as a place to sleep at night. When a house is completely demolished and becomes an open space, the name ceases to apply, and the oath is not broken. However, if only the roof is lost but the walls remain, the name persists because it can still be used for habitation. The commentator expands on this, distinguishing between 'bayt' and 'dar' and showing how a change in use affects the oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the oath
Determine whether the oath refers to 'bayt' (house) or 'dar' (dwelling). The ruling differs because 'bayt' is defined by the function of sleeping at night, while 'dar' retains its name even after destruction.
The passage focuses on 'bayt' but also discusses 'dar' in the commentary.
2
Examine the physical state of the building
Check if the building is completely demolished (becoming a field), or if only the roof is missing while walls remain. Also consider if the structure is rebuilt as a different type of building.
The state determines whether the name 'bayt' continues to apply.
3
Apply the defining characteristic of 'bayt'
Assess whether the place can still be used for sleeping at night. This is the effective cause ('illa) for the name 'bayt'. If it cannot be slept in, the name is lost.
The text explicitly states that a roof is only a description; the key is the ability to sleep.
4
Check if the name persists
If the name 'bayt' remains (e.g., walls are up), entering breaks the oath. If the name changes due to demolition or conversion to a different use (mosque, bathhouse, garden), the oath is not broken.
For 'dar', the name survives even after complete destruction, so the oath would be broken if the same structure is rebuilt.
5
Derive the ruling
State the final ruling: if the named building no longer exists as a 'bayt' (by function), entering the location does not break the oath. If it still functions as a dwelling, the oath is broken.
This ruling is based on rational reasoning (ta'lil) and the definition of terms.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اليمين في الدخول والسكنى
هذَا الْبَيْتَ فَدَخَلَهُ بَعْدَ مَا انْهَدَمَ وَصَارَ صَحْرَاءُ لَمْ يَحْنَتْ لِزَوَالِ اسْم الْبَيْتِ لأَنَّهُ لَا يُبَاتُ فِيهِ حَتَّى لوبَقِيَتِ الْحَيْطَانُ وَسَقَطَ السَّقْفُ يَحْنَتْ لأَنَّهُ يُبَاتُ فِيهِ وَالسَّقْفُ وَصْفٌ فِيهِ وَكَذَا إِذَا بُنِيَ بَيْتًا أَخَرَ فَدَخَلَهُ لَمْ يَحْنَتْ لِأَنَّ الْإِسْمَ لَمْ يَبْقَ بَعْدَ الْإِنْهِدَامِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں اس دار میں داخل نہیں ہوں گا۔ اس کے بعد وہ بالکل ویران اور کھنڈر بن گیا۔ پھر اسے دوبارہ بنا لیا گیا اس کے بعد یہ شخص اس میں داخل ہوا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ ہم پہلے بتا چکے ہیں کہ مکان ٹوٹ پھوٹ جانے کے بعد بھی اس کے دار کا نام باقی ہے (صرف وصف عمارت نہیں رہا) اور اگر ویران ہو جانے کے بعد وہ جگہ مسجد بنادی گئی یا غسل خانہ یا باغ یا کوئی کمرہ بنادیا گیا۔ پھر اس میں داخل ہوا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے اب وہ حصہ دار نہیں رہا اس لیئے اس کا نام بدل گیا ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر غسل خانہ جمام وغیرہ منہدم ہو جانے کے بعد
اس میں داخل ہوا تو بھی حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حمام وغیرہ کے ویران اور ٹوٹ پھوٹ ہو جانے کے بعد اس پر دوبارہ دار کا نام نہیں آئے گا۔ فائدہ یعنی جبکہ وہ گھر ایک نام سے متعین اور مشہور ہو چکا ہے یعنی حمام یا باغ مثلا تو اس عمارت کے گر جانے کے بعد بھی اس پر اصلی نام یعنی دار کا اطلاق نہ ہو گا۔ اور اس نام سے نہیں بولا جائے گا۔ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اس بیت میں داخل نہیں ہوگا تو پھر اس کے ویران اور میدان ہو جانے کے بعد داخل ہونے سے حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس پر سے بیت کا نام جاتا رہا ہے۔ کیونکہ اب اس میں رات کے وقت سویا نہیں جاتا ہے اور نہ کوئی سو سکتا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کی دیوار میں باقی رہ گئی ہوں اور صرف چھت گری ہو تو بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں بھی کسی طرح رات بسر کر لی جاتی ہے۔ اور چھت ہونا اس میں وصف ہے۔ اسی طرح اگر اس جگہ پر دوسرا گھر بنایا گیا پھر اس میں داخل ہوا تو بھی حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس پرائے گھر کے ختم ہو جانے کے بعد اب اس جگہ ایک نئے سبب سے نیا گھر بنا ہے۔ جبکہ اختلاف سبب سے اصل میں بھی اختلاف ہو جاتا ہے۔
Chapter on oaths regarding entry and residence. This house: he entered it after it was demolished and became a courtyard; he does not break his oath (hanith) because the name 'house' no longer applies, since it is not slept in at night. Even if the walls remain and the roof falls, he breaks his oath because it is slept in, and the roof is a description. Similarly, if another house is built and he enters it, he does not break his oath because the name did not remain after demolition. Translation: And if someone swore, 'I will not enter this house,' then it became completely ruined and desolate, then it was rebuilt, and then this person entered it, he becomes hanith. Because we have already mentioned that after a building is destroyed, the name 'dar' still remains (only the quality of construction is lost). And if after becoming ruined, that place was made into a mosque, or a bathhouse, or a garden, or a room, and then he entered it, he does not become hanith. Because now it is no longer a part of the house, so its name has changed. Similarly, if a bathhouse, etc., is demolished and then he enters it, he also does not become hanith. Because after the bathhouse becomes ruined and destroyed, the name 'dar' will not apply to it again. Benefit: That is, when a house has become defined and known by one name, like a bathhouse or garden, then after its building collapses, the original name 'dar' will not apply to it, and it will not be referred to by that name. And if someone swore, 'I will not enter this bayt,' then after it becomes ruined and a field, entering does not make him hanith, because the name 'bayt' has left it. Because now it is not slept in at night, and no one can sleep there. Even if its walls remain and only the roof has fallen, he still becomes hanith because one can still spend the night there in some way, and a roof is a description. Similarly, if another house is built on that spot and then he enters it, he does not become hanith because after the destruction of the first house, a new house has been built on that spot due to a new cause, and with a difference of cause, there is also a difference in the original [identity].
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on oaths related to entering a house (bayt or dar) when the house undergoes physical changes or change of use. The key principle is that the oath is linked to the name and identity of the subject. If the house is completely demolished and becomes an open space (sahra'), the name 'bayt' no longer applies because it cannot be used for sleeping at night—a key characteristic of a house. Therefore, entering the demolished area does not break the oath. However, if the walls remain but the roof falls, the name 'bayt' persists because it can still be used for dwelling. Similarly, if a new house is built, it is considered a different entity, so entering it does not break the original oath. The Urdu commentary adds that if the place changes into a mosque, bathhouse, or garden, the oath is not broken because the name changes completely. A important distinction: for 'dar' (house), the commentary notes that the name 'dar' survives even after destruction, unlike 'bayt' which is more specific. The criterion for 'bayt' is whether one can sleep in it at night; for 'dar', it is about the structure being a dwelling. The author uses rational reasoning (that the name depends on the function) rather than textual proof. The ruling is based on the definition of 'bayt' as a place where one spends the night (mabit). This is an example of legal reasoning (ta'lil) by identifying the effective cause ('illa) of the name.

Key Terms
بَيْت (bayt): A house that is fit for sleeping at night; its name depends on the function of habitation.
دَار (dar): A house or dwelling that retains its name even after destruction, unlike bayt which loses its name if not habitable.
حانِث (hanith): The one who breaks his oath (yamin) by committing the act he swore not to do.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, if a person swears not to enter a specific house (bayt), and then the house is completely demolished so that only an empty plot remains, what is the ruling if he enters the plot?
A) He breaks his oath (hanith) because he entered the location of the house.
B) He does not break his oath because the name 'bayt' no longer applies.
C) He breaks his oath only if the walls are still standing.
D) He does not break his oath only if the land is used for another purpose.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ties the application of an oath to enter a house to the functional identity of the building, not the physical land, so a complete change in the building's character nullifies the oath's subject.

Oath on Entering a House: Roof, Entrance Hall, and Door Archway
Explains rulings on oath regarding roof, dihliz, and taq al-bab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on oaths involving roof, dihliz, and taq al-bab, distinguishing between the standard position based on qiyas and the exception based on local custom.

Core Idea
Standing on the roof breaks the oath to not enter a house—by qiyas with the mosque roof—but custom may override.

Oaths regarding entry into a house (dar) require precise definitions of what constitutes 'entering' and what parts are considered part of the house. This lesson examines three specific scenarios: standing on the roof, entering the dihliz (entrance hall), and standing in the taq al-bab (door archway). The Hanafi position rests on qiyas with the mosque roof for i'tikaf, but later scholars also consider local custom. The door-closing criterion determines inclusion of threshold areas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of the oath
The oath uses the word 'dar' (house). Determine what elements are linguistically included in 'dar' according to the Hanafi school.
The roof is considered part of 'dar' based on linguistic usage and qiyas.
2
Apply the qiyas proof from i'tikaf
The matn analogizes the roof of a house to the roof of a mosque: just as going to the mosque roof does not invalidate i'tikaf (because the roof is part of the mosque), standing on the house roof constitutes entry into the house.
Dalil: 'Do you not see that the one in i'tikaf does not invalidate his i'tikaf by going out to the roof of the mosque?'
3
Consider the exception of custom
Some Hanafi scholars (like Faqih Abu al-Layth) hold that in non-Arab custom, the roof is not considered part of the house, so the oath is not broken. Recognize that this is a valid intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
The standard position from Zahir al-Riwayah is that the roof is included; custom-based ruling may be applied locally.
4
Analyze dihliz and taq al-bab using the door-closing criterion
For the entrance hall (dihliz) and door archway (taq al-bab), the ruling depends on whether the area is inside or outside when the door is closed. If closing the door would place the person outside, it is not part of the house.
The door serves to safeguard the house; what lies beyond a closed door is outside.
5
Note the reverse case for oaths of not exiting
If the oath is 'I will not go out of this house,' the same door-closing criterion applies in reverse: standing where the door would place you outside counts as exiting.
This shows the principle is consistent: the door's position defines the boundary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ فَوَقَفَ عَلى سَطْحِهَا حَنِثَ لاَنَّ السَّطْحَ مِنَ الدَّارِ الَا تَرَى أَنَّ الْمُعْتَكِفَ لَا يَفْسُدُ اِعْتِكَافُهُ بِالْخُرُوجِ إِلَى سَطْحِ الْمَسْجِدِ وَقِيلَ فِي عُرْفِنَا لَا يَحْنَتْ قَالَ وَإِذَا دَخَلَ دِهْلِيزَهَا يَحْنَثُ وَ يَجِبُ أَنْ يَكُونَ عَلَى التَّفْصِيلِ الَّذِي تَقَدَّمَ وَإِنْ وَقَفَ فِي طَاقِ الْبَابِ بِحَيْتُ إِذَا أُعْلِقَ الْبَابُ كَانَ خَارِجًا لَمْ يَحْنَثْ لأَنَّ الْبَابَ لِإِحْرَازِ الدَّارِ وَمَافِيهَا فَلَمْ يَكُنِ الْخَارِجُ مِنَ الدَّارِ
ترجمہ قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر کسی نے اس بات کی قسم کھائی کہ میں اس گھر میں داخل نہ ہوں گا۔ لیکن اس کی چھت پر کسی طرح کھڑا ہو گیا تو و حانث ہو گیا۔ کیونکہ گھر کی چھت بھی گھر میں داخل ہوتی ہے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ ایک اعتکاف کرنے والا اگر مسجد کے اندر سے نکل کر اس کی چھت پر چڑھ جائے تو اس کا اعتکاف فاسد نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اور کہا گیا ہے کہ ہمارے عرف و رواج میں حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس گھر کی دہلیز یعنی ڈیوڑھی میں داخل ہوا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ لیکن یہاں بھی وہی تفصیل ہونی چاہئے جو پہلے گزر چکی ہے ( یعنی اگر اس کا دروازہ بند کر دینے ہے وہ اندر کا حصہ ہو جائے اور چھت موجود ہو تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر وہ اندر کا حصہ نہ ہو سکے بلکہ باہر ہی رہ جائے تو حانث نہ ہوگا ) اور دروازے کے محرابی طاق میں اس طرح کھڑا ہوا کہ اگر دروازہ بند کر دیا جائے تو وہ باہر ہی رہ جائے تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ کیونکہ دروازہ اسی لئے ہوتا ہے کہ گھر کو اس کے اسباب سمیت محفوظ رکھا جاسکے۔ اس لئے جو حصہ اس سے باہر ہوگا وہ دار میں سے نہیں ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے قسم کھاتے ہوئے کہا لا ادخل هذه الدار ( میں اس گھر میں داخل نہ ہوں گا)۔ بعد ازاں ود باہر سے اس دار کی چھت پر کھڑا ہو گیا۔ تو حالف کی قسم ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ کیونکہ چھت بھی گھر کا حصہ ہوتی ہے۔ متن میں مذکورہ صورت مسئلہ کو مسجد کی چھت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے کہا گیا ہے کہ اگر چھت مسجد کا حصہ نہ ہوتی تو مختلف کا مسجد کی چھت پر چڑھنا مفسد اعتکاف کا سبب بنتا۔ چونکہ چھت مسجد کا حصہ ہوتی ہے، اسلئے مختلف کے اعتکاف میں فساد نقص واقع نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ دار چاردیواری اور اوپر (چھت) نیچے (فرش) پرمشتمل ہونے سے عبارت ہے۔ لہذا چھت دار کا حصہ قرار پائی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حالف اگر باہر سے دار کی چھت پر کھڑا ہو گیا۔ تو اس پر حث نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور بعض حضرات (مثل فقیہ ابواللیث ) کا قول ہے کہ ہمارے عرف ( عجم کے عرف) میں باہر سے دار کی چھت پر چڑھتے ہوئے کھڑا ہونے سے حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عجم کے عرف عام میں چھت کو دار“ کا حصہ شمار نہیں کیا جاتا۔
دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب دار کی چھت گر دی جاتی ہے۔ پھر بھی اسے دار ہی سمجھا جاتا ہے۔ اگر دار اور بیت" کے فرق کوملحوظ خاطر رکھا جائے تو اہل لغت (عرب) کا اعتبار کرنا صحیح ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ اہل عرب کے نزدیک ایک گھر“ کیلئے اس کے تمام لوازمات کا لحاظ رکھنا لازمی ہے۔ اور چھت بھی "دار" کیلئے لازمی حصہ ہے۔ اگر کوئی شخص "دار کے باہر سے رسی کے ذریعے یا درخت کے ذریعے مکان (مخلوف علیہ) پر چڑھ جائے تو متقدمین کے نزدیک حالف پرسنٹ لازما ہو گا۔ اور متاخرین کے نزدیک حانث نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن عرب و عجم دونوں کے عرف عام کا تقاضی یہی ہے کہ "دار ( جبکہ مخلوف علیہ ہو ) میں چھت کو شمار کرنا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ لفظ "دائر معنوی حیثیت کے اعتبار سے چھت کا اقتضاء کرتا ہے۔ لہذا چھت کو دار کا حصہ قرار دیا جانا چاہئے۔ اگر کسی شخص نے قسم کھاتے ہوئے یہ کہا کہ لا ادخل هذه الدار ( میں اس گھر میں داخل نہیں ہوں گا) در انحالیکہ وہ ( حالف) اس گھر کی چوکھٹ پر ایسی جگہ پر کھڑا ہو گیا کہ وہ جگہ دروازہ بند کرنے کی صورت میں گھر سے باہر شماری ہوتی ہے تو حالف ایسی صورت میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اگر وہ چوکھٹ دروازہ بند کرنے کی صورت میں گھر (دار) کے اندر شامل ہو تو حالف پر حث لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ مسئلہ کی پہلی صورت میں چوکھٹ دروازے سے باہر ہونے کی وجہ سے دار سے خارج متصور ہوگی۔ لہذا حالف پرنٹ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں چوکھٹ دروازے کے اندر شمار ہے۔ اسلئے حالف پر جٹ لازم ہوگا۔ اس کے برعکس اگر حالف نے لا اخرج هذه الدار کہا۔ تو اس صورت کا حکم بدل جائے گا۔ یعنی دروازے سے چوکھٹ باہر ہونے کی صورت میں حانث ہو گا۔ اور چوکھٹ کے دروازے کے اندر ہونے کی صورت میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مسئلہ مذکورہ کی برعکس صورت میں دروازے کی چوکھٹ باہر ہے۔ اس صورت میں حالف دار کے اندر ہی موجود ہے۔ اسلئے حالف کا وار سے خراج ثابت نہ ہوگا بخلاف لا ادخل هذه الدار کے کہ وہاں دروازے سے چوکھٹ کے باہر ہونے کی صورت میں خروج اور چوکھٹ کے اندر ہونے کی صورت میں دخول ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر حالف نے مخلوقہ دار میں اپنا سر داخل کر دیا۔ یا ایک پاؤں داخل کر دیا۔ تو بھی خانٹ نہ ہو گا۔
He said: And whoever swears, 'I will not enter this house,' and then stands on its roof, he breaks his oath (hanith) because the roof is part of the house. Do you not see that the one in i'tikaf does not invalidate his i'tikaf by going out to the roof of the mosque? And it is said in our custom: he does not break his oath. He said: And if he enters its entrance hall (dihliz), he breaks his oath, and this should be according to the detail that preceded. And if he stands in the archway of the door (taq al-bab) such that when the door is closed, he would be outside, he does not break his oath because the door is for safeguarding the house and what is in it, so what is outside is not from the house. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If someone swore, 'I will not enter this house,' but then stood on its roof in some manner, he becomes hanith. Because the roof is also part of the house. Do you not see that a person in i'tikaf, if he goes out from the mosque to its roof, his i'tikaf is not invalidated? And it has been said that in our custom, he would not be hanith. And if he enters its dihliz (porch), he becomes hanith, but here too the same detail applies as previously (i.e., if when the door is closed he is inside, he becomes hanith; if he remains outside, he does not). And if he stands in the arched niche of the door (taq al-bab) in such a way that when the door is closed he would be outside, he does not become hanith because the door is for protecting the house and its contents, so what is outside is not part of the house. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person swore 'la adkhulu hadhihi al-dar' (I will not enter this house), and afterwards he stood on its roof from outside, then his oath is broken because the roof is part of the house. The matn likens this to the roof of a mosque that is part of the mosque; if it were not part, going to it would invalidate i'tikaf. Since the roof is part of the house, standing on it from outside counts as entering. Some scholars (like Faqih Abu al-Layth) say that in our custom (the non-Arab custom), one does not break the oath because the roof is not considered part of the house in common usage. The evidence is that when the roof of a house is removed, it is still called a house. But if the distinction between 'dar' and 'bayt' is considered, relying on the Arabic language is correct, because for Arabs, a house necessarily includes all its parts, including the roof. If a person climbs onto the roof from outside via a rope or tree, the early scholars said the oath is broken, while later scholars said it is not. However, the general custom of both Arabs and non-Arabs requires that the roof be counted as part of the 'dar' when it is the subject of the oath, because the word 'dar' implies a roof. Therefore, the roof should be considered part of the house. If a person swore 'la adkhulu hadhihi al-dar' and then stood on the threshold (astanah) at a spot that, when the door is closed, would be outside the house, then he does not become hanith. If the door threshold is inside the house when closed, then he becomes hanith. In contrast, if he swore 'la akhruju min hadhihi al-dar' (I will not go out of this house), the ruling is reversed: if the threshold is outside the door, he becomes hanith when standing there (because he is considered inside), and if it is inside, he does not become hanith. Similarly, if he inserts his head or one foot into the house, he does not become hanith (for an oath of not entering).
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage covers several specific scenarios regarding oaths related to entering a house (dar). The first issue is whether standing on the roof breaks the oath. The Hanafi position, based on qiyas (analogy) with the roof of a mosque in i'tikaf, is that the roof is part of the house, so standing on it constitutes entry, breaking the oath. However, there is a reported difference: some early scholars (like Faqih Abu al-Layth) consider the local custom ('urf) of non-Arabs where the roof is not considered part of the house, so they would not break the oath. The commentary then discusses the dihliz (entrance hall) and the taq al-bab (door archway). The main criterion is whether the door can enclose the person inside when closed. If standing in a place that would be outside when the door is closed, then it is not considered part of the house. This is because the door serves to secure the house, so the area beyond the closed door is outside. The commentary also introduces the reverse case: when the oath is about not exiting the house, the same logic applies in reverse. Finally, placing only the head or foot into the house does not count as 'entering' in the sense that breaks the oath, because entrance requires the whole body or at least more than a part? Actually the text says he does not become hanith, implying that partial insertion is not sufficient to break an oath of not entering. This is a nuanced ruling specific to oaths.

Key Terms
سَطْح (sath): The roof of a house; considered part of the dar for the purpose of oaths according to the Hanafi school.
دِهْلِيز (dihliz): The entrance hall or porch of a house; its ruling depends on whether it is inside or outside the house when the door is closed.
طَاق الْبَاب (taq al-bab): The archway or niche of the door; the area that may be considered outside if the door closes outside it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears not to enter a house. He stands in the door archway (taq al-bab) such that when the door is closed, he would be outside. According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what is the outcome?
A) He breaks his oath because the archway is part of the house.
B) He does not break his oath because the area outside the closed door is not part of the house.
C) He breaks his oath only if he also enters the dihliz.
D) He does not break his oath because he did not stand on the roof.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on oaths of entry depends on whether the location is considered part of the 'dar' linguistically and by custom, with the door-closing test defining boundaries for entrance halls and archways.

Oath on Not Entering When Already Inside
Explains ruling with proof: qiyas vs. istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an oath of non-entry when already inside, and explain why istihsan overrides qiyas in this case.

Core Idea
An oath to not enter is broken only by the act of entering, not by remaining inside.

In this passage, Imam al-Quduri presents a nuanced ruling regarding oaths. A person who swears not to enter a house while already seated inside might think he must immediately leave. The Hanafi school, however, clarifies that the oath is tied to the act of entry, not the state of being inside. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, contrasting qiyas (analogy) and istihsan (juristic preference).

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the act
The text states: a person inside a house swears not to enter it. The Hanafi ruling is that he does not break the oath by remaining; he only breaks it if he leaves and re-enters. Identify the act under question: 'al-qu'ud' (sitting/remaining) is not considered 'dukhul' (entry).
The key term 'dukhul' is defined as a momentary action.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument
Qiyas would equate remaining (dawam) with beginning (ibtida'), so staying inside would be like entering. This would make the oath broken immediately. Understand the principle: 'al-baqa' ka al-ibtida''.
3
Examine the istihsan preference
Istihsan overrides qiyas based on the linguistic fact that 'dukhul' has no continuity. The act of entering is a single transition from outside to inside, not a state. Therefore, remaining does not constitute 'entry'.
This shows the Hanafi commitment to the literal meaning of words in oaths.
4
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
If the person sits inside, the oath is not broken. If he steps out and then steps back in, he breaks the oath. This is the mufta bihi position.
The phrase 'hatta yakhruja thumma yadkhula' — until he goes out and then enters.
5
Extract the usul al-fiqh lesson
This case illustrates that istihsan can override qiyas when qiyas would lead to a result contrary to the intended meaning of the text. It also highlights the importance of accurate definition of terms (dukhul).
This is a standard Hanafi approach: prioritizing semantic precision over broad analogy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ وَ هُوَ فِيْهَا لَمْ يَحْنَتْ بِالْقُعُودِ حَتَّى يَخْرُجَ ثُمَّ يَدْخُلُ إِسْتِحْسَانًا وَالْقِيَاسُ أنْ يَحْنَتْ لِاَنَّ الدَّوَامَ لَهُ حُكْمُ الْإِبْتِدَاءِ وَجْهُ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ الدُّخُولَ لَا دَوَامَ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ انْفِصَالُ مِنَ الْخَارِجِ إِلَى الداخل.
ترجمہ اور اگر اس بات کی قسم کھائی کہ اس گھر میں داخل نہ ہوں گا حالانکہ وہ اس میں موجود ہے تو جب تک وہ وہاں موجود رہے گا حانث نہ ہوگا البتہ وہاں سے نکل کر دوبارہ داخل ہونے سے استحسانا حانث ہو جائے گا کیونکہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ وہاں رہنے ہوئے حالت میں ہی حانث ہو جائے۔ اس لئے کہ کسی کام میں مداومت اور لگے رہنے کو بھی ابتداء کرنے کے جیسا حکم ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی وہاں موجود ہنا بھی نئے طور پر جانے کے برابر ہوا۔ اور استحسان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ گھر میں داخل ہونا ایسا فعل نہیں ہے کہ وہ دیر پا ہو یا اس کے لئے ہینگی ہو۔ کیونکہ باہر سے اندر کی طرف آنے کو ہی
He said: And whoever swears, 'I will not enter this house,' while he is inside it, he does not break his oath by just sitting there, until he goes out and then enters, by istihsan. And by qiyas, he would break his oath because continuance (dawam) has the same ruling as initiation (ibtida'). The face of istihsan is that 'entry' (dukhul) does not have continuance, because it is a transition from outside to inside. Translation: And if he swears, 'I will not enter this house,' while he is present in it, then as long as he remains there, he does not become hanith. However, if he goes out and then enters again, by istihsan, he becomes hanith. Because qiyas would require that he becomes hanith by merely remaining, since continuance of an action is like its initiation. The reason for istihsan is that 'entry' (dukhul) is not a continuous act; it is a momentary transition from outside to inside.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where a person already inside a house swears not to enter it. The key distinction is between the act of 'entry' (dukhul), which is a momentary action, and the state of 'being inside' (kuwn fi al-dar). According to qiyas (analogy), since he is already inside, his continued presence could be seen as a continuous form of entry, so he would be breaking the oath by remaining. However, the Hanafi ruling relies on istihsan (juristic preference) and says that the oath is not broken by staying; it is only broken if he leaves and then re-enters. The reasoning is that 'entry' (dukhul) does not have a continuous nature; it is a one-time action of crossing from outside to inside. Therefore, remaining inside does not count as 'entering'. The commentator explains that the word 'dukhul' means the act of entering, not the state of being inside. This is a subtle point of linguistic precision. The passage also notes that qiyas would have led to a different ruling, but istihsan prevails based on the understanding of the term 'dukhul'. This is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
دُخُول (dukhul): The act of entering, a momentary transition from outside to inside; not a continuous state.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas in favor of a more appropriate ruling based on linguistic or practical considerations.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; in this passage, qiyas would have led to a different ruling, but istihsan prevails.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person who is inside a house swears, 'I will not enter this house,' and then remains sitting inside, what is the ruling?
A) He breaks his oath immediately because he is inside.
B) He breaks his oath only if he leaves and comes back.
C) He breaks his oath if he remains for a long time.
D) He breaks his oath if he intends to stay.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that an oath not to enter is broken only by the act of entering, not by remaining inside, based on the linguistic precision of 'dukhul' and the principle of istihsan.

Oath of Not Entering While Inside: The Role of Istihsan and Defining the House
Ruling with proof (istihsan vs qiyas) on oath entry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that an oath not to enter is not broken by remaining inside, and determine whether standing on the roof or threshold constitutes entry.

Core Idea
A momentary act of entry cannot be extended to staying; istihsan overrides qiyas, and the definition of 'house' includes the roof and threshold depending on custom.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a common puzzle: if a person swears not to enter a house while already inside, does staying break the oath? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced ruling based on the nature of 'entry' and istihsan. The text also clarifies whether standing on the roof or threshold is considered entry, highlighting the role of custom and the literal wording of the oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main scenario and the oath
The case: someone swears 'I will not enter this house' while he is already inside. Determine what constitutes a breach (hanth) of the oath.
The oath is about the act of entering (dukhul), not about remaining (qu'ud).
2
Understand the qiyas objection
Qiyas would argue that staying (dawam) has the same ruling as initiating (ibtida'), so being inside after swearing is equivalent to entering anew, thus breaking the oath immediately.
This is the position that istihsan overrides.
3
Grasp the istihsan response
Istihsan defines dukhul as a momentary transition from outside to inside, which has no continuity (dawam). Therefore, staying does not constitute entry, and the oath is not broken until one leaves and re-enters.
The key is the linguistic and legal definition of 'entry'.
4
Apply the roof and threshold rulings
The roof is part of the house (dar) by default, so standing on it from outside breaks the oath, except where local custom excludes it. The threshold's status depends on whether it lies inside or outside the door when closed.
Custom ('urf) can modify the application, but the literal meaning governs unless custom is dominant.
5
Determine the practical result
For the main ruling: the oath is broken only by leaving and then re-entering. For roof/threshold: breaking depends on whether the location is considered part of the house according to custom and the wording of the oath.
The mufta bihi position follows istihsan for the main ruling and includes roof as part of dar unless custom dictates otherwise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اليمين في الدخول والسكنى
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو بدانید جلد ششم .. باہر سے اس دار کی چھت پر کھڑا ہو گیا۔ تو حالف کی قسم ٹوٹ جائے گی۔ کیونکہ چھت بھی گھر کا حصہ ہوتی ہے۔ متن میں مذکورہ صورت مسئلہ کو مسجد کی چھت پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے کہا گیا ہے کہ اگر چھت مسجد کا حصہ نہ ہوتی تو مختلف کا مسجد کی چھت پر چڑھنا مفسد اعتکاف کا سبب بنتا۔ چونکہ چھت مسجد کا حصہ ہوتی ہے، اسلئے مختلف کے اعتکاف میں فساد نقص واقع نہیں ہوتا۔ کیونکہ دار چاردیواری اور اوپر (چھت) نیچے (فرش) پرمشتمل ہونے سے عبارت ہے۔ لہذا چھت دار کا حصہ قرار پائی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حالف اگر باہر سے دار کی چھت پر کھڑا ہو گیا۔ تو اس پر حث نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ اور بعض حضرات (مثل فقیہ ابواللیث ) کا قول ہے کہ ہمارے عرف ( عجم کے عرف) میں باہر سے دار کی چھت پر چڑھتے ہوئے کھڑا ہونے سے حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ عجم کے عرف عام میں چھت کو دار“ کا حصہ شمار نہیں کیا جاتا۔
دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ جب دار کی چھت گر دی جاتی ہے۔ پھر بھی اسے دار ہی سمجھا جاتا ہے۔ اگر دار اور بیت" کے فرق کوملحوظ خاطر رکھا جائے تو اہل لغت (عرب) کا اعتبار کرنا صحیح ہو گا۔ اسلئے کہ اہل عرب کے نزدیک ایک گھر“ کیلئے اس کے تمام لوازمات کا لحاظ رکھنا لازمی ہے۔ اور چھت بھی "دار" کیلئے لازمی حصہ ہے۔ اگر کوئی شخص "دار کے باہر سے رسی کے ذریعے یا درخت کے ذریعے مکان (مخلوف علیہ) پر چڑھ جائے تو متقدمین کے نزدیک حالف پرسنٹ لازما ہو گا۔ اور متاخرین کے نزدیک حانث نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن عرب و عجم دونوں کے عرف عام کا تقاضی یہی ہے کہ "دار ( جبکہ مخلوف علیہ ہو ) میں چھت کو شمار کرنا چاہئے۔ کیونکہ لفظ "دائر معنوی حیثیت کے اعتبار سے چھت کا اقتضاء کرتا ہے۔ لہذا چھت کو دار کا حصہ قرار دیا جانا چاہئے۔ اگر کسی شخص نے قسم کھاتے ہوئے یہ کہا کہ لا ادخل هذه الدار ( میں اس گھر میں داخل نہیں ہوں گا) در انحالیکہ وہ ( حالف) اس گھر کی چوکھٹ پر ایسی جگہ پر کھڑا ہو گیا کہ وہ جگہ دروازہ بند کرنے کی صورت میں گھر سے باہر شماری ہوتی ہے تو حالف ایسی صورت میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اگر وہ چوکھٹ دروازہ بند کرنے کی صورت میں گھر (دار) کے اندر شامل ہو تو حالف پر حث لازم ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مذکورہ مسئلہ کی پہلی صورت میں چوکھٹ دروازے سے باہر ہونے کی وجہ سے دار سے خارج متصور ہوگی۔ لہذا حالف پرنٹ لازم نہ ہوگا۔ اور دوسری صورت میں چوکھٹ دروازے کے اندر شمار ہے۔ اسلئے حالف پر جٹ لازم ہوگا۔ اس کے برعکس اگر حالف نے لا اخرج هذه الدار کہا۔ تو اس صورت کا حکم بدل جائے گا۔ یعنی دروازے سے چوکھٹ باہر ہونے کی صورت میں حانث ہو گا۔ اور چوکھٹ کے دروازے کے اندر ہونے کی صورت میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مسئلہ مذکورہ کی برعکس صورت میں دروازے کی چوکھٹ باہر ہے۔ اس صورت میں حالف دار کے اندر ہی موجود ہے۔ اسلئے حالف کا وار سے خراج ثابت نہ ہوگا بخلاف لا ادخل هذه الدار کے کہ وہاں دروازے سے چوکھٹ کے باہر ہونے کی صورت میں خروج اور چوکھٹ کے اندر ہونے کی صورت میں دخول ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر حالف نے مخلوقہ دار میں اپنا سر داخل کر دیا۔ یا ایک پاؤں داخل کر دیا۔ تو بھی خانٹ نہ ہو گا۔
قسم اٹھائی کہ اس دار میں داخل نہیں ہوگا اور وہ اس میں تھا بیٹھنے سے حانث نہیں ہوگا
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ هَذِهِ الدَّارَ وَ هُوَ فِيْهَا لَمْ يَحْنَتْ بِالْقُعُودِ حَتَّى يَخْرُجَ ثُمَّ يَدْخُلُ إِسْتِحْسَانًا وَالْقِيَاسُ أنْ يَحْنَتْ لِاَنَّ الدَّوَامَ لَهُ حُكْمُ الْإِبْتِدَاءِ وَجْهُ الْإِسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ الدُّخُولَ لَا دَوَامَ لَهُ لِأَنَّهُ انْفِصَالُ مِنَ الْخَارِجِ إِلَى الداخل.
ترجمہ اور اگر اس بات کی قسم کھائی کہ اس گھر میں داخل نہ ہوں گا حالانکہ وہ اس میں موجود ہے تو جب تک وہ وہاں موجود رہے گا حانث نہ ہوگا البتہ وہاں سے نکل کر دوبارہ داخل ہونے سے استحسانا حانث ہو جائے گا کیونکہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ تھا کہ وہاں رہنے ہوئے حالت میں ہی حانث ہو جائے۔ اس لئے کہ کسی کام میں مداومت اور لگے رہنے کو بھی ابتداء کرنے کے جیسا حکم ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی وہاں موجود ہنا بھی نئے طور پر جانے کے برابر ہوا۔ اور استحسان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ گھر میں داخل ہونا ایسا فعل نہیں ہے کہ وہ دیر پا ہو یا اس کے لئے ہینگی ہو۔ کیونکہ باہر سے اندر کی طرف آنے کو ہی داخل ہونا کہتے ہیں جو کہ سیکنڈوں میں ہو جاتا ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے گھر میں داخل نہ ہونے کی قسم اس حال میں کھائی کہ وہ خود اس ( مخلوف علیہ ) گھر میں موجود ہے تو وہ ( حالف) اس وقت تک حانث نہ ہو گا۔ جب تک وہ اس (مخلوف علیہ ) گھر سے نکل کر دوبارہ داخل نہ ہو۔ جبکہ قیاس مقتضی ہے کہ قعود کا تسلسل لزوم حنٹ کو ثابت کرے۔ لیکن اقتضائے استحسان کے پیش نظر حالف کا قعود خروج کے بعد دوبارہ دخول سے مشروط کر دیا گیا۔ تا کہ قیاس کے اقتضاء سے قطع نظر کرتے ہوئے استحسان کا تقاضی پورا ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ قعود کا تسلسل دوام ( ہمیشگی پر مبنی ہے اور دوام ابتداء کرنے کے حکم پر مشتمل ہے۔ یعنی مسلسل قعود ایسے ہے۔ گویا کہ از سرنو جانا ہوا۔ جبکہ از سرنو جانا ہی درحقیقت ابتداء کا حکم ہے۔ چونکہ یمن میں اصولی امر یہ ہے کہ اس ( یمین ) کا انعقاد اس وقت ہوتا ہے جب یمین میں حنٹ کا وقوع متصور ہو۔ مذکورہ صورت میں یمین کا انعقاد اس وقت ہوگا جب دخول واقع ہو۔ تعود کی صورت میں دخول نہیں۔ جبکہ حث کیلئے دخول شرط ہے۔ اور شرط کا قیام مشروط (جزا) کے قیام پر موقوف ہے۔ قعود میں شرط ( دخول ) اور مشروط (حٹ ) کا وجود نہیں پایا جاتا۔ لہذا مسلسل قعود میں از سر نو جانا ہی دراصل ابتداء کے حکم پر بنی ہے۔ استحسان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ دخول وہ فعل نہیں جو دوام کا مقتضی ہو۔ اسلئے کہ قسم کھانے کے بعد گھر سے باہر نکل کر پھر داخل ہونے سے حرف مستلزم ہوگا۔ اور یہ امر آن واحد میں بھی ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کیلئے دوام ضروری نہیں اور قعود کیلئے دوام لازمی ہے۔ کلام کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ قعود کا مقتضیٰ دوام ہے اور دخول کا تقاضی آن واحد میں پورا ہو جاتا ہے۔ اس کیلئے دوام ضروری نہیں۔ چنانچہ از روئے استحسان قسم کھانے کے بعد ( پہلے سے موجود ) حالف کے خروج تک حث کو مانع قرار دیا گیا۔ بعد از خروج دخول حکم میں ابتداء کے ہوگا۔ جو کہ آن واحد میں واقع ہو کر یمین ٹوٹنے کا سبب ہوتا ہے۔
Chapter on oaths regarding entering and dwelling. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary, volume six. If he stands on the roof of that house from outside, then the oath of the swearer will be broken. Because the roof is also a part of the house. In the text, the mentioned case is analogized to the roof of a mosque: if the roof were not part of the mosque, then the madhhab's climbing onto the mosque's roof would cause a nullification of i'tikaf. Since the roof is part of the mosque, therefore the madhhab's i'tikaf does not become invalid. Because a house consists of four walls and the upper (roof) and lower (floor). Hence the roof is considered a part of the house. From this it is known that if the swearer stands on the roof of the house from outside, then the oath applies to him. And some scholars (like Faqih Abu al-Layth) say that in our custom (the custom of the non-Arabs) standing after climbing on the roof from outside does not cause breaking of the oath. Because in the common custom of the non-Arabs, the roof is not counted as part of the house. The proof of this is that when the roof of a house is demolished, it is still considered a house. If the difference between 'dar' and 'bayt' is taken into account, then relying on the lexicographers (Arabs) will be correct. Because in the view of the Arabs, it is necessary to consider all its requisites for a house. And the roof is also an integral part of the house. If a person climbs onto the house (the object of the oath) from outside by means of a rope or a tree, then according to the early scholars (mutaqaddimin) the oath is necessarily binding on the swearer. And according to the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) he does not break the oath. But the requirement of the common custom of both Arabs and non-Arabs is that when 'dar' is the object of the oath, the roof should be counted. Because the word 'dar' in its meaning necessitates the roof. Hence the roof should be considered part of the house. If a person swore saying 'I will not enter this house' (la adkhula hadhihi al-dar), and he (the swearer) stood on the threshold of that house at a place that, when the door is closed, is considered outside the house, then in such a case the swearer will not break his oath. If that threshold is included inside the house when the door is closed, then the swearer will break his oath. Because in the first case of the mentioned issue, since the threshold is outside the door, it is considered outside the house. Hence the oath does not become binding on the swearer. And in the second case, the threshold is counted inside the door. Therefore the oath becomes binding on the swearer. Conversely, if the swearer said 'I will not exit this house' (la akhruju hadhihi al-dar), then the ruling of this case is reversed: when the threshold is outside the door, he breaks the oath; and when the threshold is inside the door, he does not break the oath. Because in the reverse case of the mentioned issue, the threshold of the door is outside. In this case, the swearer is still inside the house. Therefore the swearer's exiting from the house is not established, unlike the case of 'I will not enter this house' where when the threshold is outside the door, exiting is established, and when the threshold is inside, entering is established. Similarly, if the swearer inserted his head into the house that is the object of the oath, or inserted one foot, then also he does not break the oath. He swore that he will not enter this house and he was in it: he does not break the oath by sitting. He (the author) said: And whoever swore that he will not enter this house while he is in it, he does not break the oath by sitting (qu'ud) until he goes out and then enters, as a matter of istihsan. And the qiyas would be that he breaks the oath, because continuance (dawam) has the ruling of initiation (ibtida'). The basis of istihsan is that 'entering' (dukhul) has no continuance, because it is a transition from the outside to the inside. Translation: And if he swore that he will not enter this house while he is present in it, then as long as he remains there he will not break the oath; however, if he goes out from there and then enters again, he will break the oath by istihsan, because the requirement of qiyas was that he would break the oath while staying in it. Because persistence and continuance in an action has the same ruling as doing it initially; that is, being present there is also equivalent to entering anew. And the reason for istihsan is that entering a house is not an action that is lasting or has continuity, because entering is called the movement from outside to inside, which happens in seconds. Explanation of the case: If a person swore not to enter a house while he himself is present in that (the object of the oath) house, then he (the swearer) will not break the oath until he leaves that house and enters again. While qiyas requires that the continuity of sitting (qu'ud) should establish the occurrence of breaking the oath. But in view of the requirement of istihsan, the swearer's sitting is conditioned upon entering again after exiting, so that disregarding the requirement of qiyas, the requirement of istihsan is fulfilled. Because the continuity of sitting is based on permanence (dawam), and permanence contains the ruling of initiation. That is, continuous sitting is like going anew. While going anew is in fact the ruling of initiation. Since the principle in oaths is that the oath is contracted when the occurrence of breaking (hanth) is conceivable in the oath. In the mentioned case, the oath will be contracted when entry occurs. In the case of staying, there is no entry. While breaking the oath requires entry as a condition. And the existence of the condition depends on the existence of the conditioned (the consequence). In sitting, neither the condition (entry) nor the conditioned (breaking) exists. Therefore, in continuous sitting, going anew is in fact based on the ruling of initiation. The reason for istihsan is that entry is not an action that requires continuance. Because after swearing, going out of the house and then entering again necessitates breaking the oath. And this can happen in a single moment; continuance is not necessary for it. But for sitting, continuance is necessary. The summary of the discourse is that sitting requires continuance, while entry is fulfilled in a single moment; continuance is not necessary for it. Therefore, according to istihsan, after swearing, breaking is prevented until the swearer (who was already present) leaves. After leaving, entry will be in the ruling of initiation, which occurs in a single moment and becomes the cause of the oath breaking.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (istihsan and qiyas) from the Hanafi school regarding oaths not to enter a house when the swearer is already inside. The commentary opens by discussing ancillary issues: whether standing on the roof or on the threshold constitutes entry. The author explains that the roof is part of the house, so if one swears not to enter and stands on the roof from outside, the oath is broken (except in non-Arab custom where roof is not considered part of the house per some scholars). The threshold ruling depends on whether it lies inside or outside the closed door. The main ruling is from the matn: if one swears not to enter while inside, he does not break the oath by staying (qu'ud), but only if he leaves and re-enters. This is by istihsan; qiyas would require breaking immediately because continuance (dawam) is like initiation. However, 'entry' is a momentary act, not continuous. The commentary clarifies that the oath is contracted only when entry occurs; staying is not entry. Therefore, the swearer must leave and re-enter to break the oath. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that the wording of the oath is interpreted according to its literal meaning (entry as a specific act) and istihsan prevails over qiyas when the latter would cause undue hardship.

Key Terms
دخول (dukhul): The act of entering a house, defined as a transition from outside to inside, which is momentary and has no continuity.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas when the latter leads to hardship; here, it prevents the oath from being broken by mere staying.
يمين (yamin): An oath; a legal bond that imposes an obligation to do or refrain from an action, with kaffarah upon breaking.
عرق (urf): Custom or common practice that can affect legal rulings, especially in defining terms like 'dar'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, when does a person break his oath if he swears not to enter a house while already inside?
A) Immediately upon swearing, because he is already inside.
B) When he leaves and then re-enters the house.
C) If he stays for more than a few seconds.
D) Only if he enters through the door; other means do not count.

Key Takeaway
An oath not to enter while inside is not broken by staying; only re-entry after exit triggers hanth, and the roof is part of the house unless custom dictates otherwise.
